<div id="review_81887181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81887181" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81887181?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of YA Fantasy/Paranorma/Adventure</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Penny by: </span>
      Reviewer X
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=zombies-aliens-vampires-dinos">zombies-aliens-vampires-dinos</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81887181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3084132899925248595">Quick (-ish) story: This book first came to my attention soon after it was released. I was at Borders trying to decide between three books, Strange Angels among those selections. I read the first few pages of each book in an attempt to narrow things down. Based on the prologue and the first few pages of the first chapter, Strange Angels was removed from consideration. <br/><br/>Why had I been so quick to eliminate this book from the running? Although the prologue pulled me in from the first sentence it wa</span>
  <span id="freeText3084132899925248595" style="display:none">Quick (-ish) story: This book first came to my attention soon after it was released. I was at Borders trying to decide between three books, Strange Angels among those selections. I read the first few pages of each book in an attempt to narrow things down. Based on the prologue and the first few pages of the first chapter, Strange Angels was removed from consideration. <br /><br />Why had I been so quick to eliminate this book from the running? Although the prologue pulled me in from the first sentence it was evident that the protagonist was a "tough girl", not one to be reckoned with. And while I luvz me a tough main character, particularly when said character is a girl, it only really works when written correctly. IMHO, when it comes to this genre the tough girl concept fails more often then not. I'm not sure why, exactly. Lazy and/or unimaginative writing is my best guess. But I digress.<br /><br />Fast forward to the beginning of December 2009: I had a few audible.com credits. Unfortunately there weren't any audio books I was particularly excited about. But I had a ginormous pile (read: mountain) of laundry to fold and I needed something semi-interesting to listen to while I did so. I stumbled across Strange Angels again, and for whatever reason decided to give it a go (If I remember correctly my decision had everything to do with audio book length more then any other factor, which is kind of sad, but whatever). <br /><br />Long story short(-ish): I'm glad that I chose this book. Not only was it a worthwhile use of an Audible credit, effectively keeping me entertained while folding a few weeks worth of clean laundry (in one night, might I add). But this book is a really good YA paranormal read, not to be overlooked. <br /><br />Strange Angels is the first book I've read by Lili St. Crow and it definitely won't be the last. I'm disappointed I didn't give this book a chance back when I first picked it up. I appreciate that St. Crow seemed to have a solid understand of the characters she was writing about--their history/background--before she started to write. What I mean is there are believable reasons behind the way these characters react to each other and to situations that unfold. <br /><br /> Within the last year I've read quite a few books from this exact same genre in which the characters are unrealistic in storylines that are incredibly preposterous, or worse yet, unoriginal, I was under the impression ANYONE can be published these days, so long as they write a story about a supernatural-something falling in love with a really insipid teenage girl. That being said, I can't seem to stop reading YA paranormal books which is kinda sad, I realize. But I feel the need to mention, books like Strange Angels make my addiction to this genre bearable. What I'm trying to say is this book is infinitely better then a large chunk (read: around 85%) of other books from this same genre.  <br /><br />Moving on...<br /><br />Where was I? Yes, I remember now: I really liked this book. Which is why I gave it four stars. Were I to compare this book to books from YA paranormal alone, it would definitely get five stars. <br /><br />Warning to my LDS friends: There is quite a bit of swearing in this book, but little to no sex. Actually there is no sex in this book, though there are one or two quite mild--but not exactly sexual--situations. Would I let my teenager read it? I don't know... probably. Because swearing aside, I think it's more worthwhile then any of the Twilight books. Do I think your teens should read it? Not my call. But honestly, I've always felt parents should have firsthand knowledge of what their teens are reading/watching, etc. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3084132899925248595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13379523478138976167"><i>Strange Angels</i> inhabits the same world as "Buffy the Vampire Slayer" and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely' title='Wicked Lovely by Melissa Marr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wicked Lovely</a> (and a host of others). Dru (short for ?? - we never learn exactly) is special, seeing and hearing things in the Real World that the rest of us cannot see or hear. She and her father move a lot - so often that Dru doesn't always unpack when they get to a new home. <br/><br/>The only school class we see includes a very nasty teacher (and Dru's telling the teacher off is one of those "I wish I'd said that to <i>my</i> witch-teac</span>
  <span id="freeText13379523478138976167" style="display:none"><i>Strange Angels</i> inhabits the same world as "Buffy the Vampire Slayer" and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/305234.Wicked_Lovely" title="Wicked Lovely by Melissa Marr" rel="nofollow noopener">Wicked Lovely</a> (and a host of others). Dru (short for ?? - we never learn exactly) is special, seeing and hearing things in the Real World that the rest of us cannot see or hear. She and her father move a lot - so often that Dru doesn't always unpack when they get to a new home. <br /><br />The only school class we see includes a very nasty teacher (and Dru's telling the teacher off is one of those "I wish I'd said that to <i>my</i> witch-teacher" moments) and a guy, Graves, a half-Asian Goth boy. Their partnership seems unlikely, but in one of those seemingly in-fiction-only twists they become friends, partners and (perhaps in the sequel) something more. <br /><br />Suffice it to say that I can't wait to see what happens to Dru, Graves, Christophe and how they fare in the Schola.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=psychics">psychics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1959071-kim?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46099088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13168433819373982020"><i>Strange Angels</i> is a fun start to a series that will appeal to any fan of Cassandra Clare or Scott Westerfeld . . . or the movie <i>Underworld</i>, which it more closely resembles. St. Crow delivers a tightly-written, fast-paced, novel full of paranormal action that exceeds the expectations set by the blurb on the back. I went in expecting the usual vampire/shifter/girl love triangle. And I got something so much better.<br/><br/>Despite the vampires, werewolves, zombies, etc. that inhabit St. Crow's world, at the</span>
  <span id="freeText13168433819373982020" style="display:none"><i>Strange Angels</i> is a fun start to a series that will appeal to any fan of Cassandra Clare or Scott Westerfeld . . . or the movie <i>Underworld</i>, which it more closely resembles. St. Crow delivers a tightly-written, fast-paced, novel full of paranormal action that exceeds the expectations set by the blurb on the back. I went in expecting the usual vampire/shifter/girl love triangle. And I got something so much better.<br /><br />Despite the vampires, werewolves, zombies, etc. that inhabit St. Crow's world, at the heart of this book is Dru's struggle with intimacy and the way she is forced to accept others into her life, which she is so not ready to do. Graves' and Dru's relationship makes this book, while the action keeps it moving along. But, beyond that, there's also the intriguing and unique spin that St. Crow has put on vampire lore -- one that is even better than Stephanie Meyers'. I will definitely pick up the next one in the series.</span>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review78340994">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_125471944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125471944" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125471944?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781449827595" href="/book/show/10027474-strange-angels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=boys-boys-and-not-a-girl-in-sight">boys-boys-and-not-a-girl-in-sight</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=2014-owned-challenge">2014-owned-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125471944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12338423340768746539">Bullet Review:<br/><br/>A decent book with strong characters that unfortunately gets bogged down for nearly 2/3rds of the book with Dru flailing around, not sure of what to do. Although this is good, I don't see myself checking out the rest of the series because A) there are virtually no other women (and certainly no positive female role models) in this book, B) females, once again, are cut out of being supernaturals unless they are REALLY REALLY special (the next book, Dru is the ONLY FEMALE at the schoo</span>
  <span id="freeText12338423340768746539" style="display:none">Bullet Review:<br /><br />A decent book with strong characters that unfortunately gets bogged down for nearly 2/3rds of the book with Dru flailing around, not sure of what to do. Although this is good, I don't see myself checking out the rest of the series because A) there are virtually no other women (and certainly no positive female role models) in this book, B) females, once again, are cut out of being supernaturals unless they are REALLY REALLY special (the next book, Dru is the ONLY FEMALE at the school because nearly all dhamphir are male), and C) the book closes nicely enough, there really isn't much of a sting to read on (NOT a bad thing BTW).<br /><br />I would not hesitate to recommend over similar books like "Shatter Me" (seriously, this book is nearly exactly like it, but WAY better).<br /><br />Full Review:<br /><br />Dru Anderson lives with her dad. Together, they roam the country, hunting the beings that go bump in the night. Everything is going as smoothly as things can possibly go when your livelihood involves vampires (suckers) and werewolves (werewolven) until one day, a zombie shambles into Dru's home and changes her life forever.<br /><br />Eons ago, I picked this up on sale at a used bookstore. It might have stayed on the shelf for many many more years, but for a few reasons:<br /><br />+ This year's goal is to weed through all these books I've had sitting lonesome on my shelves for years.<br />+ I also have this goal of trying to eradicate my shelves of young adult fiction, a "genre" that I am increasingly growing out of (yes, it makes me sad too).<br />+ Don't spend any more money on new books (this has been going REALLY WELL!)<br />+ If you must read a book you don't own, get an audiobook at the library.<br /><br />Whaddya know - there was an audiobook at the library! So naturally, I put this on my iPod, held my breath and dove in.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124070788" rel="nofollow noopener">This project</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916492928" rel="nofollow noopener">hasn't been</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909991360" rel="nofollow noopener">very kind to me</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/905024395" rel="nofollow noopener">as you can see</a>. At best, the books I've waded through have been "meh" or "not my thing". At worst, we have Patch.<br /><br />So when I say that "Strange Angels" is the best of the recent bunch I've waded through, it's a HUGE compliment. The writing is better, the characters are better, the world-building is better. Part of me wonders if this is because Lili St.Crow is the adult author, Lilith Saintcrow, who has already written quite a few books so is very well aware of the ropes. Part of me wonders if someone FINALLY wrote the hard-bitten, tough girl right (can't help but put in a jab at LKH and her Mary Sue, Anita Blake).<br /><br />I really liked Dru. She was a tough kid put in a sh!tty situation, and she handled it about like I imagine I would - terrified out of her mind and trying desperately to understand it. I also liked how she wasn't drop-dead gorgeous, how her first thoughts weren't about how hot the guys were around her, how she was just so NATURAL.<br /><br />I also adored Graves. In fact, I may like him more than Dru. Graves is half-Asian, and I'm just like FINALLY!!! I am SO TIRED of everyone in these novels being so blooming WHITE. (Which is why I undertook a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/749422141" rel="nofollow noopener">different project</a> to challenge my white bias.) He's a great friend, smart, resourceful, just all around NICE. I love his interactions with Dru, I love how he likes her, but isn't like, "ZOMG, lemme save you, you poor whimpering baby!" Oh, and I love how they don't fall insta-love and have time to GET TO KNOW each other (a shock, amiright?).<br /><br />The unfortunate thing is that Dru and Graves pretty much live in a world alone, until the very end when we get Christoff, a teenaged hunter (really? I mean, really?). We have Dru's dad (who is cool), but other than him, we have Dru's teacher, who is a b!tch, and that's about it. No females of note - and to make THAT worse, it's because, in this world, all the special suckers and supernatural woowoos are male. To be a female in this world is VERY VERY RARE.<br /><br />The fact that YET ANOTHER series starring a female protagonist in an almost exclusively male world (along with Mercy Thompson, Anita Blake, Merry Gentry, and many, many more) says something about us. It says that the default is male. That men are the ones to be and do special things. To be a woman and equally special, you have to be EVEN MOAR special than the men - not just the same special, but EVEN RARER. And that if a woman does become that special thing, she becomes the sole woman in a world of men. It's sad, that in the year 2014 (I know, this book was published years ago), this mentality is still very much the norm.<br /><br />Enough about the book's sexism. I have to now get into the biggest reason this is merely 3 stars and not the 4 I very much wanted to give it. And the reason is simple enough: for 2/3rds of the book, NOTHING HAPPENS.<br /><br />Oh, sure, Dru has to kill a zombie, flee werewolves (no, I refuse to call them "wolven" because that is stupid), befriend Graves, and mourn the loss of her dad (not spoiler - this happens in the first few chapters). And I didn't have a problem with this for a good 40% of the book. But by that point, I was like, "Come on, Dru. Get off your @$$ and start hitting the books." (Which she doesn't do until the 80% mark, and even then, that's one big huge ugly infodump.) By the time I got to the end where some pretty cool revelations and action scenes happen, I was so bored, I had tuned out. I didn't care what happened anymore, I wanted this book to be DONE. A shame, truly, because this book IS really good.<br /><br />And one more thing to note: while I loved the narrator, her voice for Christoff SUCKED. HARD. She like talked in Shatnerese...pausing...whenever she...felt like it might...create some...drama...for the story.<br /><br />Since this is a young adult novel, I also want to bring up some items that parents might be interested in. First off, there is a LOT of swearing in this book, and I'm taking f-bombs, not just "damn" and "hell". There aren't any objectionable sexual situations, but the violence is pretty gritty and non-stop. I would recommend for teens 16+.<br /><br />"Strange Angels" is one of the strongest vampire/urban fantasy novels in the young adult age group. It's got some great characters, great ideas, and some great action. That said, I doubt I will go further in the series because A) I've heard the end really sucks, B) I have a lot of other books to read, C) I don't have the other books in this series, D) the next book is more about how Dru is the only female in this male-centric world. Regardless of that, I would not hesitate to recommend, if you are a fan of vampires or liked the idea of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225944422" rel="nofollow noopener">"Shatter Me"</a>, but thought Juliette sucked. (Seriously, "Strange Angels" has a similar plot to "Shatter Me", but WAY better characters.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12338423340768746539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_64466506" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64466506" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2547912-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1248235253p2/2547912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64466506?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/2547912-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64466506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9595289251439954606">For me, Strange Angels didn't really work. It sounds really good, it has a good plot, strong characters and all, but then... nothing.<br/><br/>I didn't feel any real connections at all in Strange Angels. The relationships between the characters didn't feel real enough. Even some of the character traits didn't match up to the character. For example, Dru is supposedly an artist who's really good at drawing. Um, what? It's mentioned a couple times that Dru sketches and can draw really well, but it felt disjo</span>
  <span id="freeText9595289251439954606" style="display:none">For me, Strange Angels didn't really work. It sounds really good, it has a good plot, strong characters and all, but then... nothing.<br /><br />I didn't feel any real connections at all in Strange Angels. The relationships between the characters didn't feel real enough. Even some of the character traits didn't match up to the character. For example, Dru is supposedly an artist who's really good at drawing. Um, what? It's mentioned a couple times that Dru sketches and can draw really well, but it felt disjointed. I couldn't imagine Dru drawing at all. It didn't help that drawing only comes up a few times and each time it felt forced and not at all like it connected to Dru's overall character.<br /><br />I also wasn't able to relate to the characters. I mean, no one is really going to feel like Dru when her dad comes back as a zombie to kill her, or when she has to fight off some werwulf. But there are other times that, if done better, I should have been able to empathize with Dru. I didn't. I felt so detached from the book and that does make me a little sad. I wish I could have gotten into it more.<br /><br />The writing is so-so. It's readable, but it doesn't stand out. There are too many descriptions in the book, especially with describing the two love interests who's names I have now forgotten. (Which that in itself is quite sad, since I read the book only a couple days ago. The characters just aren't memorable enough.) The descriptions though, my god. I lost count how many times the eye colour of the two guys were described. I skimmed over a lot of the book because there are so many attempts at descriptions. There's also a lot of use of different verbs that sound really awkward. Of course it would be boring if the author only used simple verbs like "said" and "walk", but it just went too far in Strange Angels. It felt really forced. I'd bring up a few examples of verbs, but I had to return my copy to the library already. The verbs fall into the overly descriptive and trying too hard category.<br /><br />And because it just really bugged me, the word "hinky" was used far too much. I hadn't heard the word before, I've never heard a teenager say it. Maybe it's just me. But using "hinky" made the book seem more dated to me, or more like a hick.<br /><br />On a more positive note, the plot is interesting. The book really picked up towards the end, when a bit more is explained. In the second half or so, Dru's exceptional powers come to light, as does the actual bad guys that Dru must face.<br /><br />Overall, I like the idea of the paranormal romance. A strong heroine battling against evil while also having to deal with some love interests- sounds good. While not exactly original, it's a good idea. However, the execution was poor. The writing could have been a lot better as could the characters. The plot could also have been cleaned up.<br /><br />Still, if you haven't read it, you could pick it up. Don't bother buying it though- borrow Strange Angels from somewhere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9595289251439954606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137838591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137838591" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137838591?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-liked">books-i-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137838591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7429783734685994913">Dru Anderson has the touch, her family is all dead, and she's caught in the middle of something she doesn't understand. Her life, never normal to begin with, has now turned upside down, and the only rock in her world is a half-Asian Goth Boy she met a few days ago. This is the opening premise for Lilith Saintcrow (writing as Lili St. Crow)'s young adult series, Strange Angels.<br/><br/>Dru Anderson is not as annoying as most YA heroines these days. She has a personality, she doesn't fade into the backgrou</span>
  <span id="freeText7429783734685994913" style="display:none">Dru Anderson has the touch, her family is all dead, and she's caught in the middle of something she doesn't understand. Her life, never normal to begin with, has now turned upside down, and the only rock in her world is a half-Asian Goth Boy she met a few days ago. This is the opening premise for Lilith Saintcrow (writing as Lili St. Crow)'s young adult series, Strange Angels.<br /><br />Dru Anderson is not as annoying as most YA heroines these days. She has a personality, she doesn't fade into the background and, thank the good lord, she doesn't spend all her time worrying about her love-life, despite being stuck in the standard love triangle.<br /><br />But my personal favourite in the book, much to my surprise, was Graves. I am not generally a best friend-slash-werewolf supporter. In the war between vampire and werewolf, I am with Edward and Jean Claude every time. So imagine my astonishment when Graves totally stole my heart. I loved the way his character was portrayed, down to his babyface and his favourite "First one's free" dialogue. And I loved the way the relationship develops between him and Dru, going from indifference to helpless dependence (on both sides) to reluctant friendship and finally, to unflinching trust.<br /><br />Of course where there are werewolves, how can there be no vampires? Or in this case, half-werewolves and half-vampires. I think Lilith Saintcrow woke up one morning and thought, Yeah, that whole werewolf-vampire love triangle is so cliched, let me hedge my bets and make them half-and-half! Enter Christophe Reynard, djampir and mysterious rescuer of Dru in distress. I cannot tell a lie, I like Christophe, too. He's an arrogant know-it-all, mysterious so-and-so, but Saintcrow could have done a better job with him. He is unnecessarily cryptic, and refuses to equip Dru with vital information that could save her life, despite his self-styled guardian angel designation. And please, what was that, with the whole fighting over the keys to the car thing? Dusk is approaching, so are the suckers, imminent death is staring them all in the face, and they want to argue about who gets to drive the car? Please, give me a break.<br /><br />The book also gets annoying in parts when the narrative becomes incomprehensibly disjointed. I understand that stream-of-consciousness writing tends to be a little uneven, but the reader still needs to know what happened. And I found Dru's coping mechanism — repress all painful thoughts, then cry about them, then repress them again — unbearably irritating sometimes. And the way she keeps repeating her questions, even when she knows she's not going to get any answers. And some of her questions are SO lame.<br /><br />All in all, this book is definitely worth a read, although I don't know if I'll be reading it again any time soon. But at least I'm moving on to books two and three, which is a sort-of -positive recommendation for the series in and of itself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7429783734685994913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_132745051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132745051" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593498-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323494878p2/4593498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132745051?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/4593498-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No One</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      A friend
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132745051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1876390712842305157">It's been awhile since I read this book, but I hated it so much that I have to review it.<br/><br/>This book was a major disappoinment. I wanted to read the book so bad because the plot sounded similar to my favorite tv show Supernatural, a show the originally started out centered around two hunter brothers that had lost their mother to a demon but later evolved to include angels and demons. The show is fantastic, unlike this book. The annoying thing is, the book has MAJOR potential to be amazing and if o</span>
  <span id="freeText1876390712842305157" style="display:none">It's been awhile since I read this book, but I hated it so much that I have to review it.<br /><br />This book was a major disappoinment. I wanted to read the book so bad because the plot sounded similar to my favorite tv show Supernatural, a show the originally started out centered around two hunter brothers that had lost their mother to a demon but later evolved to include angels and demons. The show is fantastic, unlike this book. The annoying thing is, the book has MAJOR potential to be amazing and if only the plot was more developed and the characters less annoying.<br /><br />First off, the main character, the teenage girl, who's name I can't even remember, is a major crybaby. She talks herself up so much that you think she is some badass hunter, but she isn't. She's just an annoying and unrelatable wus. It seems as if every other chapter she just bawls her eyes out over her dead father. I understand having a character crying once or twice, weakness makes characters believable and enhaces the plot, but seriously, the girl cries way to much and just adds to the stereotypical emotional female persona. <br /><br />Secondly, the plot is very hard to follow. The book just doesn't transition well from event to event. It was rocky, confusing, and generally annoying considering it was coupled with the protagonist's unending crying. It seemed like there was no point to most of the story and that it just wasn't going anywhere.<br /><br />Finally, in one part of the story, the girl's newly made best friend is described as something like "a halfy" or along those lines. This confused me to no end. Was the boy a human-vampire halfbreed? I later read that another reviewer thought this refered to his half-Asian appearance, which made much more sense.<br /><br />Overall, do not waste your time with this book, especially if you are annoyed with today's lack of strong female characters. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1876390712842305157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_56684475" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56684475" />
    <a title="Katie(babs)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs"><img alt="Katie(babs)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242522005p2/179852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56684475?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie(babs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie(babs)" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs">Katie(babs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56684475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10291273151181931222">Dru Anderson and her father move from place to place ever since Dru’s grandmother died. Dru’s father is a hunter. He goes out at night and kills supernatural beings such as poltergeists, werewulfs and vampires, or as Dru likes to call them, suckers. He has been doing this since Dru’s mother passed away when she was a little girl. Dru is not really sure what happened to her mother because her father and grandmother kept her in the dark about her mother. Sometimes Dru is her father’s backup. She i</span>
  <span id="freeText10291273151181931222" style="display:none">Dru Anderson and her father move from place to place ever since Dru’s grandmother died. Dru’s father is a hunter. He goes out at night and kills supernatural beings such as poltergeists, werewulfs and vampires, or as Dru likes to call them, suckers. He has been doing this since Dru’s mother passed away when she was a little girl. Dru is not really sure what happened to her mother because her father and grandmother kept her in the dark about her mother. Sometimes Dru is her father’s backup. She is skilled in all types of combat and knows how to use a gun and can take down a body with her self-defense moves. Dru longs to be like any other sixteen year old who goes to school, dates and practice her sketching. Dru is also a very angry girl and she is at the point where she has no motivation. She has given up on life; she doesn’t seem to care what she wears or what she looks like. She goes through each day like a zombie.<br /><br />Dru and her father have left Florida and now reside for the time being in the Dakotas. The weather is fierce here because it is cold, snowy and desolate. One morning Dru sees a white owl. This owl shows up whenever someone is going to die or something bad is going to happen. The night Dru’s grandmother died, the owl appeared. Dru should tell her father about the owl, but she stops herself. Lately she is not sure what to do or say to her father. Mr. Anderson only cares about confronting these evil things. He is on a mission and Dru isn’t sure what he hopes to accomplish. Dru leaves her father to it, even though deep down she is scared and has a feeling she won’t see him again. She will soon find out how right her intuition is.<br /><br />The world is a stage for Dru and she must put on an act in school. She tries to remain anonymous and not bring attention to herself. But there is one student who zones in on Dru. He is Graves, a half-Asian goth kid who wants to befriend her for no reason Dru can think of. She just wants to be alone and tries her best to get rid of Graves. Graves is a bit like a puppy dog and wants attention. Dru does long for a friend to confide in. But how can she tell this strange boy that she and her father travel around the states, hunting things that go bump in the night, killing things you only find in fairy tales and ghost stories? Because of these travels, Dru is empty and knows in a few months she will be moving on and will only have her father as her companion.<br /><br />When Dru returns home, her father is missing. This is not the norm and Dru knows something bad has happen to her dad. Her father does return, but as a flesh dripping zombie. Dru has no choice but to shoot her zombie dad. She is now alone and has no one to turn to. But up pops Graves who won’t be ignored. He becomes a big support for Dru and will help her get through her pain and suffering. Graves is going to wish he never met Dru because the things that go bump in the night are after Dru. One of those nasty creatures, a werewulf tracks Dru and attacks her. Graves gets caught in the crossfire and is bitten by the wulf. Dru has to make a tough decision about Graves because if he turns into a wulf, she will have to kill him just like she did her father.<br /><br />Surprisingly, Graves doesn’t turn all furry even though he does have some residual effects form the bite. Graves wants to help Dru figure out why she is being targeted. Help comes in the form of Christophe Reynard, a half-breed vampire called a djamhir who is the member of the secret Order. Christophe knows all about Dru’s family and what really happened to her mother and why her father was turned into a zombie. Dru doesn’t understand how special she is. When Dru comes into her maturity and into her powers she has always ignored, she could become a powerful tool to the Order. Dru is shocked to learn that she comes from a line of vampires.<br /><br />There is one who wants to eliminate Dru, just as he did with her mother. He is Sergei, one of the oldest Princeps or vampire around and the one Dwight Anderson has been hunting for twelve long years. For the longest time Dru has only relied on herself to survive, but now she must trust Christophe who seems to have all the answers but is not upfront as he should be. He is mysterious in his own right and has his own plans for Dru. Graves won’t leave Dru and feels they now have a connection after all they have gone through. Dru has never had a normal life to begin with but this new turn of events will place her in even more peril. She has no where to turn and unless she allows Christophe to take charge, she will end up like her parents.<br /><br />Strange Angels is a very dark and morbid young adult novel. There are different levels to young adult books in regards to subject matter and the suitable age for young readers. The inside of the book says this Lili St. Crow book is for ages twelve and up. I feel that Strange Angels is more suited for the high school crowd and definitely not for a seventh grader. There is just too much violence and some issues with the terms of language. I feel a twelve year old is still very much a child and too young to read a book such as this.<br /><br />I am all for dark and angsty paranormals and Strange Angels delivers this. There are fight scenes between many supernatural baddies. Blood is shed and guns are blazing. When the action is all said and done, what we have is a very desolate tale in the eyes of the tormented Dru Anderson. Dru is written in such a way where she is a bit bitchy. She is one of those people who would snarl at you and is almost a bit rabid in the way she acts. Perhaps this is understandable because her mother was murdered and her father lives by the gun and wants to rid the world of evil. Dru is along for the ride and has no choice in the matter. She has been isolated and can barely keep up appearances or is comfortable in public. Because Dru has such a harsh personality, I couldn’t find myself connected to her in any way. I felt pity for the girl because of the life she had been forced into.<br /><br />There is no hope or joy for Dru. She comes across as an abuse victim, someone who has been pushed to the side and has never felt love or feels she should be loved. Dru’s world is one I would not want to be aware or a part of. For the life of me I could not see why Graves would be so interested in Dru. She comes across as a lost soul, one that cannot be rescued. Graves may be her guardian angel, but he will have to go through hell and back for her. Graves is the reason to read Strange Angels. He brings such light and hope into a story like this. But I can’t help but wonder if Dru will suck away some of his innocence and hope for a future. Christophe is an interesting addition even though I felt Lili was trying a bit too hard when it came to him. He is too one-dimensional for my tastes and if Lili is trying to plant the seeds of a love triangle between Christophe, Dru and Graves, I would say Graves has already come out on top. Unfortunately I would want someone much better for Graves than the morbid Dru.<br /><br />Violence and angst are two perfect words to explain Lili St. Crow’s Strange Angels. The way things end may make you want to continue to read on and see if Dru survives and if she is able to handle everything that comes her way. Due to my own feelings toward Dru and the desolate feeling I had after I finished, I would say I take a pass on the next book in what I assume will have a sequel.<br /><br />I will give credit to St. Crow for channeling a bit of George Romero’s Dawn of the Dead. There are a few scenes where Graves and Dru have run of the local mall. I felt this had a great atmospheric feel, much like the one I felt when watching a George Romero zombie movie. Romero’s zombie horror movies also give off the vibe of hopelessness and Lili has done exactly this with Strange Angels. I think that is where my own fault lies because sometimes a book can just be too depressing and dark to really have a good reading experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10291273151181931222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

	<tr>
		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wsK46P3oIru+M35Nh2rMPzgl+xvyCRT2xUm01zkOewi2kvTAXWuSxqixzia5MywWjl7+A2TobmCK5HWA4rLycQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('la/X1TzfUAZc0/8oywHqiwavaGQi++liS+jkqI46OTbh/5v9nFzge0pRT0P1WAqisNRtfLQak/QERSX/VYawTw==')})
  }
